< review>
Moved into the facility this past Saturday (4/9/16) with some items. We are relocating down south from Northern California in phases. The facility location seems good and good security.

When we opened our unit to start unloading we noticed two spots inside where rodents had gnawed their way through, probably moving from one unit to another.

My husband told the front desk immediately and they said they had extermination services on it.

We went ahead and moved in and as we did we noticed some rodent droppings on the floor. We are unsure how old they are.

After working incredibly hard to pack, load and travel the 4 hours to get there in pouring rain, we were too tired to switch gears to go look for another facility. We chose to take the managers word for it but have since been worried and uneasy.

We are withholding our review of the facility in a more positive light, until we feel really confident that the manager is really on top of it, as he said he is.

Sadly we will need to take a day now, that we really don't have, to drive down there to check on it, to make sure the manager is really 'on-top' of it.<//review>

<review>We really enjoyed this venue for our December wedding. We originally planned to have our ceremony at a different location but we had to change last minute because of the weather but ended up being able to have our ceremony outside on the patio area. The greenery surrounding the patio is nice so we were happy with that backdrop. We had the dinner inside and it was definitely intimate with 56 guests. I'm glad we ended up with that number because with any more people it probably would have felt crowded. The bridal room is very small, we did not use it to get ready, but even with storing some of our bags and other items it was cramped. You have to use an approved caterer. We used Culinary Excellence and they were great! There is not a full kitchen on-site though so they were cooking in a tent out in the parking area. This venue allows beer & wine only, no liquor. (Translated by Google) The fountain created by the Canadian artist Armand Vaillancourt officially bears the name "Quebec Libre!".
The idea for a fountain by Vaillancourt came from the imagination of Lawrence Halprin, a well-known landscape architect. In 1968 he announced that the fountain to be created by Vaillancourt would be considered one of America's "great works of civil art". After the installation of the artwork in 1971, however, the (expected) criticism did not fail to materialize.
Vaillancourt himself saw his work as a confrontational work that could serve as a magnet for protest and contradiction.
It should be noted that Interstate 480 thundered past here in 1971. The area has long since been redeveloped and the Bay Area has become a highly frequented area.
At first sight the fountain appears like a chaotically thrown pile of square concrete pipes. However, the chaos is not accidental, it was thought through by the artist to the place where it should be. Today it is provocatively free, the relieving newly built highway standing on pillars in the back. From this perspective, the fountain itself is ideally placed in the picture. Usually, however, you stand directly in front of the plant, which is up to 12 m high. From this perspective, the challenge is of course different, putting it in the sense of the construction, maybe confusing at the moment.
I personally like the cubic work from all perspectives.

<Review>Like many establishments, they've setup outdoor dining. Menu is a code to scan on the table. We enjoyed a couple of new items on the menu. The half rack ribs with shrimp and 2 sides and the half rack ribs with chicken. Sauce had a nice flavor, bit too spicy or too sickly sweet. Meat was "fall off the bone" cooked. Coleslaw was crispy fresh, not too vinegary. Also had fries, and that is where plating issues come in. If you put a bunch of fries on the plate and then a rack of hot, juicy, BBQ ribs on top of them, what's going to happen to fries. The ones underneath are soft and soggy. The coleslaw came in a separate small dish which kept it's juice from spreading out underneath the fries as well.
But overall, it was a very good lunchtime break and I would recommend it.<//Review>< Pics>

<Rate>2</Rate>< review>
I use to go to the Coco's in La Mesa all the time, it was wonderful! Unfortunately they closed 2 years ago and I am forced to come here. I usually like them but I had a poor experience on Thanksgiving.

I called to see if they were doing slices of pie because, my mom was in the hospital for the holiday unexpectedly and that was all she wanted and I had already driven around town. Apparently pie is some huge secret because, Katie could not tell me what pies they had. I did the drive all the way down to Coco's from the hospital in Mission Valley only to find out they didn't even make the pie I was looking for. I had told Katie my situation on the phone, I didn't want to make a drive for a pie that didn't exist. She made it seem as if this pie was there. Once I talked to her again and told her what was going on she said, "aww poor baby." very sarcastically, insincere and dismissive. I wanted to cry because, it's just my mom and I living here in San Diego and I'm just a kid trying to manage all of this and give my mom a holiday meal while she's in the hospital.

Once I got into the back area where they were distributing pies (I figured I'd just buy a whole pie, take a slice and give the rest away). They didn't have much left by noon but told me to come back in 4 hours, that's a sick joke. I did talk to a nice woman working and told her my story and she was so sweet about the situation and made recommendations. Miraculously the slice of pie that KATIE told me didn't exist showed up! I appreciated the lady who helped me and another gentleman (guest) for helping me out but I felt that Katie was playing with people's emotions and I didn't appreciate it whatsoever.

Not surprised by Katie's dismissive attitude because, I witnessed her one time saying something explicit to a cook in Spanish. She even admitted it and asked if I spoke Spanish and heard her.</review>
